Performs double thresholding on an image 

Applies double thresholding algorithm to segment image into three regions\+: strong edges (above high threshold), weak edges (between thresholds), and non-\/edges (below low threshold)


\begin{DoxyParams}{هڈ‚و•°}
{\em input} & Input image \\
\hline
{\em output} & Output thresholded image \\
\hline
{\em low\+\_\+threshold} & Lower threshold value (default 20) \\
\hline
{\em high\+\_\+threshold} & Higher threshold value (default 50) \\
\hline
{\em strong\+\_\+pixel} & Strong edge pixel value (default 255) \\
\hline
{\em weak\+\_\+pixel} & Weak edge pixel value (default 128) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{perception@{perception}!imGetContours@{imGetContours}}
\index{imGetContours@{imGetContours}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{imGetContours()}{imGetContours()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::im\+Get\+Contours (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{cv\+::\+Mat}]{input,  }\item[{cv\+::\+Mat \&}]{output,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ std\+::vector$<$ cv\+::\+Point $>$$>$ \&}]{contours,  }\item[{int}]{mode,  }\item[{int}]{method }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Finds contours in a binary image 

Uses Open\+CV\textquotesingle{}s find\+Contours function to detect contours in a binary image. The input image should be binary (thresholded). The function detects edges and outputs contours as vector of points.


\begin{DoxyParams}{هڈ‚و•°}
{\em input} & Input binary image \\
\hline
{\em contours} & Output vector of detected contours, where each contour is a vector of points \\
\hline
{\em mode} & Contour retrieval mode (default\+: C\+V\+\_\+\+R\+E\+T\+R\+\_\+\+E\+X\+T\+E\+R\+N\+AL) \\
\hline
{\em method} & Contour approximation method (default\+: C\+V\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+I\+N\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+R\+O\+X\+\_\+\+S\+I\+M\+P\+LE) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::im\+Get\+I\+PM (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const cv\+::\+Mat \&}]{in\+Image,  }\item[{cv\+::\+Mat \&}]{out\+Image,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{structperception_1_1IPMInfo}{I\+P\+M\+Info}} $\ast$}]{ipm\+Info,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structperception_1_1CameraInfo}{Camera\+Info}} $\ast$}]{camera\+Info,  }\item[{std\+::list$<$ cv\+::\+Point $>$ $\ast$}]{out\+Points }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Coordinate system description 

We are assuming the world coordinate frame center is at the camera, the ground plane is at height -\/h, the X-\/axis is going right, the Y-\/axis is going forward, the Z-\/axis is going up. The camera is looking forward with optical axis in direction of Y-\/axis, with possible pitch angle (above or below the Y-\/axis) and yaw angle (left or right). The camera coordinates have the same center as the world, but the Xc-\/axis goes right, the Yc-\/axis goes down, and the Zc-\/axis (optical cxis) goes forward. The uv-\/plane of the image is such that u is horizontal going right, v is vertical going down. The image coordinates uv are such that the pixels are at half coordinates i.\+e. first pixel is (.5,.5) ...etc where the top-\/left point is (0,0) i.\+e. the tip of the first pixel is (0,0)

Generates Inverse Perspective Mapping of input image 
\begin{DoxyParams}{هڈ‚و•°}
{\em in\+Image} & Input image to transform \\
\hline
{\em out\+Image} & Output I\+PM transformed image \\
\hline
{\em ipm\+Info} & I\+PM parameters and info for the transformation \\
\hline
{\em camera\+Info} & Camera calibration parameters \\
\hline
{\em out\+Points} & Optional list to store indices of points outside image bounds\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

Finds intersection of image plane with line in X\+Y-\/plane making yaw angle with Y-\/axis

Computes the vanishing point in the image plane uv. It is the point of intersection of the image plane with the line in the X\+Y-\/plane in the world coordinates that makes an angle yaw clockwise (form Y-\/axis) with Y-\/axis

\index{imScharrTrans@{imScharrTrans}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{imScharrTrans()}{imScharrTrans()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::im\+Scharr\+Trans (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{cv\+::\+Mat}]{input,  }\item[{cv\+::\+Mat \&}]{output,  }\item[{double}]{scale,  }\item[{double}]{delta }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Applies Scharr edge detection operator to an image 

The Scharr operator is used for edge detection and is more accurate than Sobel for edge detection, particularly for edges at 45 degrees. It computes both x and y derivatives and combines them.


\begin{DoxyParams}{هڈ‚و•°}
{\em input} & Input image (grayscale) \\
\hline
{\em output} & Output edge detected image \\
\hline
{\em scale} & Optional scale factor for derivatives (default 1) \\
\hline
{\em delta} & Optional value added to results (default 0) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{perception@{perception}!pcdAffinityPropagationCluster@{pcdAffinityPropagationCluster}}
\index{pcdAffinityPropagationCluster@{pcdAffinityPropagationCluster}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pcdAffinityPropagationCluster()}{pcdAffinityPropagationCluster()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::pcd\+Affinity\+Propagation\+Cluster (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{pcl\+::\+Point\+Cloud$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+X\+YZ $>$\+::Ptr}]{input,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+Indices $>$ \&}]{cluster\+\_\+indices,  }\item[{float}]{damping,  }\item[{int}]{max\+\_\+iterations,  }\item[{int}]{convergence\+\_\+threshold }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs Affinity Propagation clustering on a P\+CL point cloud. 

This function implements the Affinity Propagation algorithm, which identifies clusters by selecting exemplars through message passing (responsibility and availability) based on point similarity. It uses squared Euclidean distance as the similarity metric and outputs clusters as point indices.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{هڈ‚و•°}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em input} & Pointer to the input point cloud (X\+Y\+ZI format). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em cluster\+\_\+indices} & Vector of Point\+Indices containing the resulting clusters. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em damping} & Damping factor (0.\+5 to 1.\+0) to stabilize convergence. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+iterations} & Maximum number of iterations to run the algorithm. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em convergence\+\_\+threshold} & Number of iterations with no exemplar change to stop early. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{و³¨è§£}
Similarity is computed as negative squared Euclidean distance; no pre-\/set cluster count needed. 

Requires a non-\/empty input cloud; otherwise, cluster\+\_\+indices will be empty. 
\end{DoxyNote}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceperception_a48030bb7ff113939c9480e35634ffbf9}\label{namespaceperception_a48030bb7ff113939c9480e35634ffbf9}} 
\index{perception@{perception}!pcdBIRCHCluster@{pcdBIRCHCluster}}
\index{pcdBIRCHCluster@{pcdBIRCHCluster}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pcdBIRCHCluster()}{pcdBIRCHCluster()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::pcd\+B\+I\+R\+C\+H\+Cluster (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{pcl\+::\+Point\+Cloud$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+X\+Y\+ZI $>$\+::Ptr}]{input,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+Indices $>$ \&}]{cluster\+\_\+indices,  }\item[{int}]{branching\+\_\+factor,  }\item[{float}]{max\+\_\+distance }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs B\+I\+R\+C\+H-\/like clustering on a P\+CL point cloud. 

This function implements a simplified version of the B\+I\+R\+CH clustering algorithm, which hierarchically clusters points based on spatial proximity. It uses a Kd\+Tree for efficient nearest-\/neighbor searches and groups points into clusters based on a branching factor and distance threshold. The output is a vector of point indices representing the clusters.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{هڈ‚و•°}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em input} & Pointer to the input point cloud (X\+Y\+ZI format). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em cluster\+\_\+indices} & Vector of Point\+Indices containing the resulting clusters. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em branching\+\_\+factor} & Maximum number of subclusters in a node (controls granularity). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em max\+\_\+distance} & Maximum distance between points to be in the same cluster. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{و³¨è§£}
B\+I\+R\+CH typically uses a C\+F-\/tree, but this is a simplified adaptation using P\+CL tools. 

Requires a non-\/empty input cloud; otherwise, cluster\+\_\+indices will be empty. 
\end{DoxyNote}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceperception_a94aa8b3dd4889b73902dc9c8e8db41bc}\label{namespaceperception_a94aa8b3dd4889b73902dc9c8e8db41bc}}

\index{pcdMeanShiftCluster@{pcdMeanShiftCluster}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pcdMeanShiftCluster()}{pcdMeanShiftCluster()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::pcd\+Mean\+Shift\+Cluster (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{pcl\+::\+Point\+Cloud$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+X\+Y\+ZI $>$\+::Ptr}]{input,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+Indices $>$ \&}]{cluster\+\_\+indices,  }\item[{float}]{bandwidth,  }\item[{int}]{max\+\_\+iter }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs mean-\/shift clustering on a point cloud 

Uses mean-\/shift algorithm to cluster points by iteratively shifting points towards local density maxima


\begin{DoxyParams}{هڈ‚و•°}
{\em input} & Input point cloud to be clustered \\
\hline
{\em cluster\+\_\+indices} & Output vector containing indices for each cluster \\
\hline
{\em bandwidth} & Kernel bandwidth parameter that determines the size of the window used to compute mean shift \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+iter} & Maximum number of iterations for mean shift convergence\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{و³¨è§£}
The algorithm works by\+:
\begin{DoxyEnumerate}
\item For each point, calculating weighted mean of nearby points within bandwidth
\item Shifting the point towards the weighted mean
\item Repeating until convergence or max iterations reached
\item Points that converge to the same mode are grouped into clusters 
\end{DoxyEnumerate}
\end{DoxyNote}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceperception_a5a00fb9f380eeec73c84a041fb2a30a5}\label{namespaceperception_a5a00fb9f380eeec73c84a041fb2a30a5}}

\index{pcdOPTICSCluster@{pcdOPTICSCluster}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pcdOPTICSCluster()}{pcdOPTICSCluster()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::pcd\+O\+P\+T\+I\+C\+S\+Cluster (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{pcl\+::\+Point\+Cloud$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+X\+Y\+ZI $>$\+::Ptr}]{input,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+Indices $>$ \&}]{cluster\+\_\+indices,  }\item[{float}]{eps,  }\item[{int}]{min\+Pts }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs O\+P\+T\+I\+CS clustering on a P\+CL point cloud. 

This function implements the O\+P\+T\+I\+CS (Ordering Points To Identify the Clustering Structure) algorithm, a density-\/based clustering method that orders points based on reachability distances and identifies clusters of varying densities. It uses a Kd\+Tree for efficient nearest-\/neighbor searches and outputs clusters as point indices.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{هڈ‚و•°}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em input} & Pointer to the input point cloud (X\+Y\+ZI format). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em cluster\+\_\+indices} & Vector of Point\+Indices containing the resulting clusters. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em eps} & Maximum distance (epsilon) for points to be considered neighbors. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em min\+Pts} & Minimum number of points required to form a core point. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{و³¨è§£}
This is a simplified O\+P\+T\+I\+CS implementation; full O\+P\+T\+I\+CS typically produces a reachability plot, but here we extract clusters directly using a basic threshold approach. 

Requires a non-\/empty input cloud; otherwise, cluster\+\_\+indices will be empty. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\index{perception@{perception}!pcdWardCluster@{pcdWardCluster}}
\index{pcdWardCluster@{pcdWardCluster}!perception@{perception}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{pcdWardCluster()}{pcdWardCluster()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void perception\+::pcd\+Ward\+Cluster (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{pcl\+::\+Point\+Cloud$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+X\+Y\+ZI $>$\+::Ptr}]{input,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ pcl\+::\+Point\+Indices $>$ \&}]{cluster\+\_\+indices,  }\item[{int}]{num\+\_\+clusters }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Performs Ward\textquotesingle{}s hierarchical clustering on a P\+CL point cloud. 

This function implements Ward\textquotesingle{}s method, a hierarchical clustering algorithm that minimizes the increase in within-\/cluster variance when merging clusters. It uses squared Euclidean distance and a Kd\+Tree for efficient distance calculations. The process continues until the desired number of clusters is reached.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{هڈ‚و•°}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em input} & Pointer to the input point cloud (X\+Y\+ZI format). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em cluster\+\_\+indices} & Vector of Point\+Indices containing the resulting clusters. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em num\+\_\+clusters} & Desired number of final clusters (must be $>$= 1 and $<$= point count). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{و³¨è§£}
This is a simplified implementation; full Ward\textquotesingle{}s method typically builds a dendrogram, but here we stop at a specified number of clusters. 

Requires a non-\/empty input cloud; otherwise, cluster\+\_\+indices will be empty. 
\end{DoxyNote}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespaceperception_a230d519122cf223841aa30278fd12c34}\label{namespaceperception_a230d519122cf223841aa30278fd12c34}}
